<Review>For Thanksgiving, 2013, I ordered a complete turkey dinner from this Bel Air at a cost of about $60 for my friend and me.   The pictures in the brochure of it and the other choices, such as rack of lamb, looked wonderful.  The Bel Air staffer who took my order told me all that was necessary was to warm everything up for an hour and a half and dinner would be ready.  Therefore, my friend and I were shocked to find the stuffing, which was minimal and tasteless, had to be mixed with a bag of liquid and a bag of celery and also placed in the over.   The directions said we should put a meat thermometer in the turkey to watch for 325 degrees,   We wondered why this would be necessary, since we didn't have one and weren't told we needed one, but at the end of the "warm-up" period, when I tried to slice the turkey, it was tough and pink in the center!   There was a limp sack of plain mashed potatoes, a sack of plain gravy, a small sack of cranberry apple, and a pumpkin pie.  No vegetable, no salad, no yams.   It was an unpleasant surprise to both of us that the Raley's organization would do such a poor job!</Review>< Pictures>

<text>Adobe Books is a longstanding SF hub for artists, vagabonds, and the curious. With over 25 years in the Mission, they've fostered a diverse community of collaborators and supporters who stood with the establishment when they were on the verge of being obliterated from map.

<userid>105262747009404301662<//userid>< username>
Dha</username>
< Text>
We found this place by accident but love it.  The food is fresh.  Tortillas made fresh on the spot.  Beef is top notch.  Service reminds me of the "Soup Nazi" on Seinfeld.  After entering the door, make sure you promptly get in line,  decide how many tacos you want and let the lady know when asked (because she will only make the tortilla fresh and to order) then decide quickly what meat you want and clearly tell the lady/man when asked, then move along the counter to the condiments,  then again be clear and precise about what you want on your tacos, then move to the cashier to pay.  If they are really busy , you will probably won't see any smiles. But the owner, sometimes come around and say hi.  Overall, very efficient process.  So worth a visit, especially on Tuesdays.  Honest reviewer.<//Text>

< Review>
Absolutely amazing I was reluctant since it didn't look to authentic but to my surprise it is and a healthier alternative to greasier tacos with two tortillas. Meat is great quality and not too salty perfectly seasoned, tortillas are made fresh to order and they actually have a bigger salsa and almost salad bar since they have fine cabbage, lettuce and great guacamole that actually is real you can see and taste the avocados and not all the other stuff they typically add. Plenty of lemons and carrots in escabeche. Tuesday tacos are on sale or a taco plate for $5.99 with your choice of beans and rice. I suggest the black beans and white rice. And plenty of cold plain water!</Review>

< Text>
I've eaten here about eight-or-nine times now on my lunch breaks and every meal has been superb, as well as the customer service. Each meal has tasted amazing. They really do have fresh and quality ingredients. It can seem a bit on the pricier end (around $8.00 for a burrito), but it is money well spent. It's great portions without being excessive (like a Chipotle burrito), so you don't feel stuffed and gorged afterward. Also, they have great veggie options - the substitute beef and chicken are just as flavorful as the meat counterparts. I highly recommend giving this place a try.</Text>

< review>
It was a very good Mexican restaurant, a long ways better than say Chipotle or Qdoba.

The man working at the taco bar was extremely friendly and good customer service never goes unnoticed by me. I had a fish taco plate which, while on a slightly pricier side, used fresh tilapia, justifying the bump in price. It was fresh, well seasoned, and hot from the grill as I could see it being made, and generally all of it was very fresh. Great quality. Go to this place of Chipotle's lack of consistency and quality bums you out.< /review>
